<p>The most notable collections of Rembrandt's work are at Amsterdam's <a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum_Amsterdam" class="mw-redirect" title="Rijksmuseum Amsterdam">Rijksmuseum</a>, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_Watch" title="The Night Watch">The Night Watch</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jewish_Bride" title="The Jewish Bride">The Jewish Bride</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Mauritshuis" title="Mauritshuis">Mauritshuis</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">Hermitage Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery" title="National Gallery">National Gallery</a> in London, <a href="/wiki/Gem%C3%A4ldegalerie,_Berlin" title="Gemäldegalerie, Berlin">Gemäldegalerie</a> in Berlin, <a href="/wiki/Gem%C3%A4ldegalerie_Alte_Meister" title="Gemäldegalerie Alte Meister">Gemäldegalerie Alte Meister</a> in Dresden, <a href="/wiki/The_Louvre" class="mw-redirect" title="The Louvre">The Louvre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nationalmuseum,_Stockholm" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalmuseum, Stockholm">Nationalmuseum, Stockholm</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Schloss_Wilhelmsh%C3%B6he" title="Schloss Wilhelmshöhe">Schloss Wilhelmshöhe</a> in Kassel. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle,_Warsaw" title="Royal Castle, Warsaw">Royal Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> displays two paintings by Rembrandt.<sup id="cite_ref-zamek_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zamek-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable collections of Rembrandt's paintings in the USA are in the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frick_Collection" title="Frick Collection">Frick Collection</a> in New York City, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Art" title="National Gallery of Art">National Gallery of Art</a> in Washington, D.C.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt_House_Museum" title="Rembrandt House Museum">Rembrandt House Museum</a> in central Amsterdam in the house he bought at the height of his success, has furnishings that are mostly not original, but period pieces comparable to those Rembrandt might have had, and paintings reflecting Rembrandt's use of the house for art dealing. His printmaking studio has been set up with a printing press, where replica prints are printed. The museum has a few Rembrandt paintings, many loaned, but an important collection of his prints, a good selection of which are on rotating display. All major <a href="/wiki/Print_room" title="Print room">print rooms</a> have large collections of Rembrandt prints, although as some exist in only a single impression, no collection is complete. The degree to which these collections are displayed to the public, or can easily be viewed by them in the print room, varies greatly.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_works">Selected works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rembrandt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Selected works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrandt_Girl_in_a_Picture_Frame.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Rembrandt_Girl_in_a_Picture_Frame.jpg/170px-Rembrandt_Girl_in_a_Picture_Frame.jpg" width="170" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Rembrandt_Girl_in_a_Picture_Frame.jpg/255px-Rembrandt_Girl_in_a_Picture_Frame.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Rembrandt_Girl_in_a_Picture_Frame.jpg/340px-Rembrandt_Girl_in_a_Picture_Frame.jpg 2x" data-file-width="664" data-file-height="900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrandt_Girl_in_a_Picture_Frame.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Girl in a Picture Frame</i>, 1641, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle,_Warsaw" title="Royal Castle, Warsaw">Royal Castle, Warsaw</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_049.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_049.jpg/170px-Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_049.jpg" width="170" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_049.jpg/255px-Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_049.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_049.jpg/340px-Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_049.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2024" data-file-height="2509" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rembrandt_Harmensz._van_Rijn_049.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The evangelist Matthew and the angel</i>, 1661</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Stoning_of_Saint_Stephen" title="The Stoning of Saint Stephen">The Stoning of Saint Stephen</a></i> (1625) – <small><a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Fine_Arts_of_Lyon" title="Museum of Fine Arts of Lyon">Musée des Beaux-Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a></small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Andromeda_Chained_to_the_Rocks" title="Andromeda Chained to the Rocks">Andromeda Chained to the Rocks</a></i> (1630) – <small><a href="/wiki/Mauritshuis" title="Mauritshuis">Mauritshuis</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a></small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Jacob_de_Gheyn_III" title="Jacob de Gheyn III">Jacob de Gheyn III</a></i> (1632) – <small><a href="/wiki/Dulwich_Picture_Gallery" title="Dulwich Picture Gallery">Dulwich Picture Gallery</a>, London</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Philosopher_in_Meditation" title="Philosopher in Meditation">Philosopher in Meditation</a></i> (1632) – <small><a href="/wiki/The_Louvre" class="mw-redirect" title="The Louvre">The Louvre</a>, Paris</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Anatomy_Lesson_of_Dr._Nicolaes_Tulp" title="The Anatomy Lesson of Dr. Nicolaes Tulp">The Anatomy Lesson of Dr. Nicolaes Tulp</a></i> (1632) – <small><a href="/wiki/Mauritshuis" title="Mauritshuis">Mauritshuis</a>, The Hague</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Artemisia_(Rembrandt)" title="Artemisia (Rembrandt)">Artemisia</a></i> (1634) – <small>Oil on canvas, 142 × 152&#160;cm, <a href="/wiki/Museo_del_Prado" title="Museo del Prado">Museo del Prado</a>, Madrid</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Descent_from_the_Cross_(Rembrandt,_1634)" title="The Descent from the Cross (Rembrandt, 1634)">Descent from the Cross</a></i> (1634) – <small>Oil on canvas, 158 × 117&#160;cm, looted from the <a href="/wiki/Landgrave" title="Landgrave">Landgrave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Landgraviate_of_Hesse-Kassel" title="Landgraviate of Hesse-Kassel">Hesse-Kassel</a> (or Hesse-Cassel), Germany in 1806, currently <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">Hermitage Museum</a>, St. Petersburg</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Belshazzar%27s_Feast_(Rembrandt)" title="Belshazzar's Feast (Rembrandt)">Belshazzar's Feast</a></i> (1635) – <small><a href="/wiki/National_Gallery" title="National Gallery">National Gallery</a>, London</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Prodigal_Son_in_the_Tavern" class="mw-redirect" title="The Prodigal Son in the Tavern">The Prodigal Son in the Tavern</a></i> (c. 1635) – <small>Oil on canvas, 161 × 131&#160;cm <a href="/wiki/Gem%C3%A4ldegalerie_Alte_Meister" title="Gemäldegalerie Alte Meister">Gemäldegalerie Alte Meister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a></small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Dana%C3%AB_(Rembrandt_painting)" title="Danaë (Rembrandt painting)">Danaë</a></i> (1636–1643) – <small><a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">Hermitage Museum</a>, St. Petersburg</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_Watch" title="The Night Watch">The Night Watch</a></i>, formally <i>The Militia Company of Captain Frans Banning Cocq</i> (1642) – <small><a href="/wiki/Rijksmuseum" title="Rijksmuseum">Rijksmuseum</a>, Amsterdam</small></li>
<li><i>Christ Healing the Sick</i> (<a href="/wiki/Etching" title="Etching">etching</a> c.&#160;1643, also known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Hundred_Guilder_Print" title="Hundred Guilder Print">Hundred Guilder Print</a></i>)<small>, nicknamed for the huge sum paid for it</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Boaz_and_Ruth_(paintings)" title="Boaz and Ruth (paintings)">Boaz and Ruth</a></i> (1643) aka <i>The Old Rabbi</i> <i>Old Man</i> – <small><a href="/wiki/Woburn_Abbey" title="Woburn Abbey">Woburn Abbey</a>/<a href="/wiki/Gemaldegalerie,_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Gemaldegalerie, Berlin">Gemaldegalerie, Berlin</a></small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Mill_(Rembrandt)" title="The Mill (Rembrandt)">The Mill</a></i> (1645/48) – <small><a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Art" title="National Gallery of Art">National Gallery of Art</a>, Washington,&#160;D.C.</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Old_Man_with_a_Gold_Chain" title="Old Man with a Gold Chain">Old Man with a Gold Chain</a></i> ("<i>Old Man with a Black Hat and Gorget</i>") (c. 1631) <small><a href="/wiki/Art_Institute_of_Chicago" title="Art Institute of Chicago">Art Institute of Chicago</a></small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Susanna_and_the_Elders_(Rembrandt)" title="Susanna and the Elders (Rembrandt)">Susanna and the Elders</a></i> (1647) – <small>Oil on panel, 76 × 91&#160;cm, <a href="/wiki/Gem%C3%A4ldegalerie,_Berlin" title="Gemäldegalerie, Berlin">Gemäldegalerie, Berlin</a></small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Aristotle_Contemplating_a_Bust_of_Homer" class="mw-redirect" title="Aristotle Contemplating a Bust of Homer">Aristotle Contemplating a Bust of Homer</a></i> (1653) – <small><a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a>, New York</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Bathsheba_at_Her_Bath_(Rembrandt)" title="Bathsheba at Her Bath (Rembrandt)">Bathsheba at Her Bath</a></i> (1654) – <small>The Louvre, Paris</small></li>
<li><i>Christ Presented to the People (Ecce Homo)</i> (1655) – <small>Drypoint, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Museum_of_Art" title="Birmingham Museum of Art">Birmingham Museum of Art</a></small></li>
<li><i>Selfportrait</i> (1658) – <small><a href="/wiki/Frick_Collection" title="Frick Collection">Frick Collection</a>, New York</small></li>
<li><i>The Three Crosses</i> (1660) Etching, fourth state</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ahasuerus_and_Haman_at_the_Feast_of_Esther" title="Ahasuerus and Haman at the Feast of Esther">Ahasuerus and Haman at the Feast of Esther</a></i> (1660) – <small><a href="/wiki/Pushkin_Museum" title="Pushkin Museum">Pushkin Museum</a>, Moscow</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Conspiracy_of_Claudius_Civilis" title="The Conspiracy of Claudius Civilis">The Conspiracy of Claudius Civilis</a></i> (1661) – <small><a href="/wiki/Nationalmuseum" title="Nationalmuseum">Nationalmuseum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gaius_Julius_Civilis" title="Gaius Julius Civilis">Claudius Civilis</a> led a Dutch revolt against the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>) (most of the cut up painting is lost, only the central part still exists)</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Portrait_of_Dirck_van_Os" title="Portrait of Dirck van Os">Portrait of Dirck van Os</a></i> (1662) - <small><a href="/wiki/Joslyn_Art_Museum" title="Joslyn Art Museum">Joslyn Art Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha, Nebraska</a></small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Syndics_of_the_Drapers%27_Guild" title="Syndics of the Drapers' Guild">Syndics of the Drapers' Guild</a></i> (Dutch <i>De Staalmeesters</i>, 1662) – <small>Rijksmuseum, Amsterdam</small></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Jewish_Bride" title="The Jewish Bride">The Jewish Bride</a></i> (1665) – <small>Rijksmuseum, Amsterdam</small></li>
<li>"The Entombment Sketch" (c. 1639 and reworked c. 1654) oil on oak panel <small><a href="/wiki/Hunterian_Museum_and_Art_Gallery" title="Hunterian Museum and Art Gallery">Hunterian Museum and Art Gallery</a>, Glasgow</small></li>
<li><i>Saul and David</i> (ca. 1660–1665) – <small><a href="/wiki/Mauritshuis" title="Mauritshuis">Mauritshuis</a>, The Hague</small></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Exhibitions">Exhibitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rembrandt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Exhibitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>Feb 12, 2015 – May 17, 2015: <i>Late Rembrandt</i>, The Rijksmuseum, Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></li>
<li>Oct 15, 2014 – Jan 18, 2015: <i>Rembrandt: The Late Works</i>, The National Gallery, London.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li>Oct 19, 2014 – Jan 4, 2015: <i>Rembrandt, Rubens, Gainsborough and the Golden Age of Painting in Europe</i>, Jule Collins Smith Museum of Art.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li>May 19, 2014 – Jun 27, 2014: <i>From Rembrandt to Rosenquist: Works on Paper from the NAC's Permanent Collection</i>, National Arts Club.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li>Sep 16, 2013 – Nov 14, 2013: <i>Rembrandt: The Consummate Etcher</i>, Syracuse University Art Galleries.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></li>
<li>Apr 21, 2011 – Jul 18, 2011: <i>Rembrandt and the Face of Jesus</i>, Musée du Louvre.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rembrandt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-BY-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-BY_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BY_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BY_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Or possibly 1607 as on 10 June 1634 he himself claimed to be 26 years old. See <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.codart.nl/news/82/">Is the Rembrandt Year being celebrated one year too soon? One year too late?</a> and <span class="languageicon">(in Dutch)</span> J. de Jong, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nd.nl/artikelen/2006/februari/03/rembrandts-geboortejaar-een-jaar-te-vroeg-gevierd">Rembrandts geboortejaar een jaar te vroeg gevierd</a> for sources concerning Rembrandts birth year, especially supporting 1607. However, most sources continue to use 1606.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/rembrandt">"Rembrandt"</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160304200247/http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/rembrandt">Archived</a> 4 March 2016 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.. <i><a href="/wiki/Random_House_Webster%27s_Unabridged_Dictionary" title="Random House Webster's Unabridged Dictionary">Random House Webster's Unabridged Dictionary</a></i>.</span></li>

(Dover Publications, 1971, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0486299414" title="Special:BookSources/0486299414">0486299414</a> ), p. 98</span></li>

(Wipf &amp; Stock, 2013, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781625641090" title="Special:BookSources/9781625641090">9781625641090</a>)</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This version of his first name, "Rembrandt" with a "d," first appeared in his signatures in 1633. Until then, he had signed with a combination of initials or monograms. In late 1632, he began signing solely with his first name, "Rembrant". He added the "d" in the following year and stuck to this spelling for the rest of his life. Although we can only speculate, this change must have had a meaning for Rembrandt, which is generally interpreted as his wanting to be known by his first name like the great figures of the Italian Renaissance: Leonardo, Raphael etc., (who did not sign with their first names, if at all). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rembrandt-signature-file.com/">Rembrandt-signature-file.com</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160409172243/http://www.rembrandt-signature-file.com/">Archived</a> 9 April 2016 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.</span></li>

The British Museum is due to publish a new catalogue after a similar exercise.</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-50">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mendelowitz, Daniel Marcus: <i>Drawing</i>. (New York: Holt, Rinehart &amp; Winston, Inc., 1967), p. 305. As Mendelowitz (1967) noted: "Probably no one has combined to as great a degree as Rembrandt a disciplined exposition of what his eye saw and a love of line as a beautiful thing in itself. His "Winter Landscape" displays the virtuosity of performance of an Oriental master, yet unlike the Oriental calligraphy, it is not based on an established convention of brush performance. It is as personal as handwriting."</span></li>
